## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / materials science constitutive modeling (thermo-mechanical stress–strain relations)
**Analysis**: The variables map directly to a constitutive law where stress (sigma) depends on strain (epsilon) and temperature (T). Common relationships include elastic modulus and yield/flow stress being temperature-dependent, plus thermoelastic shifts due to thermal expansion.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law with temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear thermoelastic stiffness approximation)
- Exponential modulus softening: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (stiffness changes strongly with T over a range)
- Polynomial modulus model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (empirical E(T) fit for a phase/temperature window)
- Thermoelastic strain offset (thermal expansion): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (stress from mechanical strain after subtracting thermal strain)
- Nonlinear elastic (cubic) with temperature-dependent stiffness: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**3 (weak-to-moderate nonlinearity)
- Ramberg–Osgood-type implicit stress–strain (explicit rearranged form): sigma = c0 * epsilon / (1 + c1 * Abs(epsilon)**c2) (smooth transition from linear to nonlinear compliance)
- Ludwik/Hollomon hardening with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * Abs(epsilon)**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (strain hardening modulated by temperature)
- Power-law hardening with thermal expansion shift: sigma = (c0 + c1 * Abs(epsilon - c2 * (T - c3))**c4) (mechanical strain measured relative to thermal strain)
- Saturating hardening (Voce-like): sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(c2 * Abs(epsilon))) (hardening saturates at large strain; c2 typically negative)
- Thermally softened Voce hardening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(c2 * Abs(epsilon)))) * exp(c3 * T) (flow stress decreases/increases systematically with T)
- Johnson–Cook (no strain-rate term): sigma = (c0 + c1 * Abs(epsilon)**c2) * (1 - c3 * (T - c4)**c5) (empirical plastic flow with thermal softening referenced to c4)
- Smooth elastic–plastic transition with temperature-dependent yield: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon * (c2 + (1 - c2) * tanh(c3 * Abs(epsilon) + c4 * T)) (blends elastic slope into plastic-like response; c2 sets low-strain weight)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Small-strain linear regime → sigma proportional to epsilon with a T-dependent slope (interpretable as E(T))
- Thermal expansion induces an intercept/shift → dependence on (epsilon - c * (T - T0)) rather than epsilon alone
- Thermal softening of strength/modulus → multiplicative factor decreasing with T such as exp(c * T) with c < 0 or (1 - c * (T - T0)**m)
- Strain hardening in plasticity → sigma grows with Abs(epsilon)**n or with (1 - exp(c * Abs(epsilon))) to represent saturation
- Different tension/compression response or sign-invariant plastic flow → use Abs(epsilon) in hardening/flow-stress terms
- Rapid property changes near transitions (e.g., phase change) → higher-order T terms (T**2, T**3) or sharp sigmoidal-in-T blends (tanh(c*T + c0))
- Coupled thermo-mechanical effects → allow coefficients of epsilon, epsilon**3, or hardening terms to be linear/polynomial in T
- Yield-like onset without explicit piecewise rules → smooth blending using tanh(c*Abs(epsilon) - c0) to emulate an elastic-to-plastic switch

Variable-wise, ε drives the decaying exponential (c1=-0.279), the dominant linear trend (c2≈5.07e3), and the logarithm (c6≈1.02), while T appears only in the mild multiplier exp(c5T) with small |c5| (≈-0.00148), so for moderate T this factor is near 1. Parameter values show near-cancellation of the constant and exponential prefactor (c3≈-c0), making the first block effectively c0( exp(-0.279ε)−1 ), and the log term contributes a negative correction of magnitude ≈900·exp(-0.00148T)·log(1+1.02ε). Thus the fitted model is approximately c2·ε + c0( exp(-0.279ε)−1 ) − 898.6·exp(-0.00148T)·log(1+1.0235ε), consistent with the extremely low NMSE.

The GT has three basis functions: **ε²**, **T·log(ε+1)**, and **log(ε+1)**.

Let me check each candidate systematically.

**Key structural requirements:** The candidate must be able to produce:
1. An ε² term (quadratic in ε)
2. A T·log(ε+1) term (product of T and log)
3. A log(ε+1) term

Let me go through candidates, focusing on whether they can generate these basis functions.

This gives T*c0 (linear in T, no ε dependence) but GT needs T*log(ε+1). T*c0 alone cannot produce T·log(ε+1).

### Candidate 12: c0*ε/(c1+|ε|) + c2*log(c3*ε+1)/(c1+|ε|) + c4*ε*exp(c5/(T+c6))/(c1+|ε|) + c7*log(c3*ε+1)*|ε|/(c1+|ε|) + c8*ε*exp(c5/(T+c6))*|ε|/(c1+|ε|)

For ε≥0, |ε|=ε, c1+|ε|=c1+ε. Everything divided by (c1+ε).

Let me set c1=0. Then 1/|ε| = 1/ε for ε>0:
- c0*ε/ε = c0
- c2*log(c3*ε+1)/ε
- c4*ε*exp(c5/(T+c6))/ε = c4*exp(c5/(T+c6))
- c7*log(c3*ε+1)*ε/ε = c7*log(c3*ε+1)
- c8*ε*exp(c5/(T+c6))*ε/ε = c8*ε*exp(c5/(T+c6))

T-dependence is exp(c5/(T+c6)), not T. Cannot produce T·log(ε+1).
Candidate 12 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 40: T*c0*log(c1*ε+1)*|ε|/(c2+|ε|) + T*c3*log(c1*ε+1)/(c2+|ε|) + c4*log(c5*ε+1)/(c2+|ε|) + c6*ε/(c2+|ε|) + c7*log(c5*ε+1)*|ε|/(c2+|ε|)

For ε≥0: everything divided by (c2+ε). Let me set c2=0:
- T*c0*log(c1*ε+1)*ε/ε = T*c0*log(c1*ε+1) ✓ This gives T·log!
- T*c3*log(c1*ε+1)/ε - problematic (1/ε singularity)

Let me try c2≠0 instead. Factor out 1/(c2+ε):
= [T*c0*log(c1*ε+1)*ε + T*c3*log(c1*ε+1) + c4*log(c5*ε+1) + c6*ε + c7*log(c5*ε+1)*ε] / (c2+ε)

GT*(c2+ε) = (90.776ε² + 2.482·T·log(ε+1) - 838.769·log(ε+1))·(c2+ε)

Expanding GT*(c2+ε):
= 90.776·c2·ε² + 90.776·ε³ + 2.482·c2·T·log(ε+1) + 2.482·T·ε·log(ε+1) - 838.769·c2·log(ε+1) - 838.769·ε·log(ε+1)

The numerator of candidate 40 has terms: T·ε·log, T·log, log, ε, ε·log. 
But GT*(c2+ε) has ε³ and ε² terms that cannot be produced by the candidate's numerator. No polynomial terms of degree ≥2 in the numerator.

Candidate 40 verdict: [NO MATCH]
